               </div>
               
               
               
               <div class="article-section__table-footnotes">
                  <ul>
                     <li id="pssb202400272-note-0001" class="footNotePopup__item" title="Footnote 1"><span class="number">a) </span>
                        
                        Fixed position.
                        </li>
                  </ul>
               </div>
               <div class="article-section__table-source"></div>
            </div>
            
            <p>XRD measurements were carried out to compare the phase composition of the MoS<sub>2</sub>/rGO powder and the discharged working electrode. In the 2Θ range of 5°–38°, the XRD pattern of the powder exhibits (002) and (100) reflections from the 2 H-MoS<sub>2</sub> lattice (curve 1 in Figure <a href="#pssb202400272-fig-0008">8c</a>). The average number of MoS<sub>2</sub> layers estimated from the broadening of the (002) reflection is 4.7, which is consistent with TEM data. The very weak intensity of the (002) graphite reflection around ≈25.6° indicates that the rGO layers are poorly ordered along the <i>c</i>-axis and are highly defective.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#pssb202400272-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="pssb202400272-bib-0040_R_d128824295e1658" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Carbon">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> According to XRD analysis of the used electrode material, sodium intercalation makes the initial rather crystalline MoS<sub>2</sub> nanosheets highly disordered, since no sharp reflection peaks are observed, except for one attributed to PVDF (curve 2 in Figure <a href="#pssb202400272-fig-0008">8c</a>). The observed small broad reflection around 7.3° ± 1.3° corresponds to an interlayer spacing of 1.0 to 1.5 nm. An increase in the interlayer distance was previously reported for commercial 2 H-MoS<sub>2</sub> and the interlayer spacing was found to be ≈0.72 nm as a result of Na ion intercalation at cell voltages up to 0.2 V.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#pssb202400272-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="pssb202400272-bib-0006_R_d128824295e1671" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - ACS Nano">6</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
            
            <p>The binding energies of 161.2 eV for the S 2p<sub>3/2</sub> component and 228.0 eV for the Mo 3d<sub>5/2</sub> component (Table 1) correspond to the values obtained for metastable tetragonal 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> phase.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#pssb202400272-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="pssb202400272-bib-0041_R_d128824295e1684" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - Nat. Mater.">41</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> A change in the local coordination of molybdenum with sulfur atoms from trigonal prismatic in the 2H phase to octahedral in the 1T phase leads to a change in splitting of the 4d orbitals.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#pssb202400272-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="pssb202400272-bib-0042_R_d128824295e1690" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - Sci. Rep.">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Incomplete occupation of the degenerated Mo 4d orbital in 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> makes this compound metallic, which is accompanied by a down-shift of in the binding energy of Mo 3d and S 2p electrons as compared to the semiconducting 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#pssb202400272-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="pssb202400272-bib-0043_R_d128824295e1699" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - ACS Nano">43</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> It has been previously shown that adding electrons to 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> stimulates the formation of the 1T phase.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#pssb202400272-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="pssb202400272-bib-0005_R_d128824295e1707" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - ChemSusChem">5</a>-<a href="#pssb202400272-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="pssb202400272-bib-0007_R_d128824295e1707" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Nano Energy">7</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In our case, the source of these electrons is sodium intercalated between the MoS<sub>2</sub> layers. Analysis of the XPS data reveals that about 21% of MoS<sub>2</sub> retained in the original hexagonal structure. Considering that the number of MoS<sub>2</sub> layers in the MoS<sub>2</sub>/rGO hybrid is about five on average, the remaining structurally untransformed MoS<sub>2</sub> layer is most likely in direct contact with the graphene component, which prevents the change in the arrangement of sulfur atoms relative to molybdenum.</p>
            
            <p>Thus, ex situ XRD analysis of the MoS<sub>2</sub>/rGO electrode showed that the first introduction of Na<sup>+</sup> ions leads to disordering of the initial 2H crystallites. XPS study of the discharged electrode revealed a partial change in the local coordination of molybdenum from the initial to tetragonal. Metallic molybdenum formed as a result of the conversion reaction was not detected in the electrode material. Previous XRD<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#pssb202400272-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="pssb202400272-bib-0006_R_d128824295e1730" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - ACS Nano">6</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and XANES<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#pssb202400272-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="pssb202400272-bib-0009_R_d128824295e1735" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Energy Storage Mater.">9</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> studies of sodiation of MoS<sub>2</sub> reported the formation of a 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> phase after the first deep discharge of the electrode and did not report the persistence of MoS<sub>2</sub> with the trigonal prismatic molybdenum coordination characteristic of 2H phase. The latter event in our case may be associated with a strong interaction between the components of the MoS<sub>2</sub>/rGO hybrid.</p>
            </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="pssb202400272-sec-0007">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="pssb202400272-sec-0007-title">3 Conclusions</h2>
         
         <p>MoS<sub>2</sub>/rGO nanomaterial was synthesized by rapid decomposition of a mixture of (NH<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>MoS<sub>4</sub> and graphene oxide at 600 °C. TEM images of the synthesis product showed MoS<sub>2</sub> nanosheets coating wrinkled graphene layers. According to XRD, the number of adjacent MoS<sub>2</sub> layers is about five, a very weak and broad (002) graphite reflection indicated a large disorder of the graphene layers. The nanomaterial was used as a working electrode in a sodium-ion half-cell to study its electronic structure upon interaction with Na<sup>+</sup> ions. A special cell with a transparent, conductive, and robust window was developed to record XANES and XES spectra. Analysis of the spectra revealed partial oxidation of sulfur and molybdenum even in a freshly assembled cell due to the contact of MoS<sub>2</sub> with the reaction products of a metallic sodium and the NaClO<sub>4</sub>/EC/DMC electrolyte. Operando XANES and in situ XES measurements of the cell detected a significant decrease in the density of unoccupied S 3p and Mo 4d states and their shift toward lower energies due to electron density donation from intercalated sodium. An XPS study of the discharged electrode showed the formation of a surface SEI layer and the reconstruction of most hexagonal MoS<sub>2</sub> layers into tetragonal layers. MoS<sub>2</sub> layers that retain their original structure are most likely in direct contact with the rGO surface, which prevents their transformation even when the electrode is completely discharged. Thus, the proper combination of nanostructured MoS<sub>2</sub> with a graphene-like component can ensure stable performance of the hybrid electrode material in SIBs.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="pssb202400272-sec-0008">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="pssb202400272-sec-0008-title">4 Experimental Section</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="pssb202400272-sec-0009">
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="pssb202400272-sec-0010">
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="pssb202400272-sec-0011">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="pssb202400272-sec-0011-title"> Materials</h4>
                  
                  <p>Purified natural graphite was oxidized using a modified Hummer's method. Details of the synthesis procedure and the results of product characterization are given in.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#pssb202400272-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="pssb202400272-bib-0044_R_d128824295e1803" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - J. Struct. Chem.">44</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> (NH<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>MoS<sub>4</sub> was synthesized by passing H<sub>2</sub>S gas through an ammonia solution of (NH<sub>4</sub>)<sub>6</sub>Mo<sub>7</sub>O<sub>24</sub>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#pssb202400272-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="pssb202400272-bib-0018_R_d128824295e1826" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">18</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The synthesis of the MoS<sub>2</sub>/graphene hybrid was carried out as following: (NH<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>MoS<sub>4</sub> and graphite oxide, taken in a mass ratio of 2.44, were dispersed in water and the suspension was freeze-dried to obtained an aerogel, which was put in a vertical quartz reactor filled with argon and heated to 600 °C. After 20 s of synthesis, the reactor was removed from the oven and the resulting product was cooled naturally in an argon environment.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="pssb202400272-sec-0012">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="pssb202400272-sec-0012-title"> Instrumental Methods</h4>
                  
                  <p>SEM and TEM images were obtained on a field emission CIQTEK SEM5000 microscope and a Jeol JEM-2200FS microscope, respectively. The sample for TEM study was prepared by ultrasonic dispersion of powder suspended in ethanol on a colloidal carbon substrate. XRD patterns were taken on a Shimadzu XRD-7000 diffractometer using Cu Kα radiation. Raman scattering was recorded using a LabRAM HR Evolution spectrometer and excitation with an Ar<sup>+</sup> laser at a wavelength of 514 nm. XPS spectra were collected at room temperature on a FlexPS SPECS spectrometer using monochromatic Al Kα radiation (1486.71 eV) with an incidence angle of 54.7<sup>o</sup>. At the used pass energy of 20 eV, the energy resolution of the spectrometer was ≈0.45 eV measured at the Ag 3d<sub>5/2</sub> line. The sp<sup>2</sup> C 1s peak at 284.6 eV was used to calibrate the binding energy.</p>
                  
                  <p>XES spectra were acquired using a laboratory high-vacuum X-ray spectrometer “Stearate”. An X-ray tube with a copper anode operated at a voltage of 10 kV and a current of 0.4 A. S Kα<sub>1,2</sub> and Mo Lα<sub>1,2</sub> spectra were obtained using a crystal SiO<sub>2</sub> (2d = 6.68637 Å). The spectra were recorded using a proportional counter filled with 10% methane and 90% argon. The resulting spectra were the average of ten scans. The energy scale of the S Kα<sub>1,2</sub> spectra was calibrated to the positions of Kα<sub>2</sub> component at 2307.39 eV and Kα<sub>1</sub> component at 2308.64 eV for the CaSO<sub>4</sub> reference,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#pssb202400272-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="pssb202400272-bib-0045_R_d128824295e1874" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - J. Phys. B: At. Mol. Opt. Phys.">45</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> while the Mo Lα<sub>1,2</sub> spectra were calibrated using 2293.16 eV for Lα<sub>1</sub> and 2289.85 eV for Lα<sub>2</sub> of metallic Mo powder.</p>
                  
                  <p>XPS and XES spectra were fitted by a combination of Gaussian and Lorentzian functions using Casa XPS software, Version 2.3.15. The position accuracy of the spectral components was 0.01–0.20 eV.</p>
                  
                  <p>The XANES S K-edge and Mo L<sub>3</sub>-edge spectra were measured using a synchrotron radiation from the VEPP-4M accelerator complex located at the Budker Institute of Nuclear Physics SB RAS.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#pssb202400272-bib-0046" class="bibLink tab-link" id="pssb202400272-bib-0046_R_d128824295e1893" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 46 - Phys. Procedia">46</a>, <a href="#pssb202400272-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="pssb202400272-bib-0047_R_d128824295e1893" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - J. Surf. Investig. X-Ray, Synchrotron Neutron Tech.">47</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The spectra of the powders were recorded in transmission mode, while the spectra of batteries were obtained in fluorescence yield mode using precision Si photodiode SPD.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#pssb202400272-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="pssb202400272-bib-0048_R_d128824295e1898" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48">48</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> During the measurements, the electron beam current varied within 15–3 mA, and the electron energy was ≈2.5 GeV. A two-crystal Si(111) monochromator with an energy resolution (ΔE/E) = 1 × 10<sup>−4</sup> was used. The battery was discharged during experiment by a potentiostat Elins P-8nano. The energy scale of the XANES spectra was calibrated by the position of the S K-edge spectra of elemental sulfur at 2472.4 eV and CaSO<sub>4</sub> at 2482.6 eV. The spectra were processed in the ATHENA program (IFEFFIT software package).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#pssb202400272-bib-0049" class="bibLink tab-link" id="pssb202400272-bib-0049_R_d128824295e1908" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 49 - J. Synchrotron Radiat.">49</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> After subtracting the linear pre-edge and the three-term (quadratic) polynomial postedge background, the spectra were normalized to the unity edge jump. The XANES spectra measured for the sodium-ion half-cells were smoothed.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="pssb202400272-sec-0013">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="pssb202400272-sec-0013-title"> Cell Assembly and Electrochemical Measurements</h4>
                  
                  <p>Electrochemical cells were assembled in an argon-filled glove box. The active material, conductive additive SuperP, and binder polyvinylidene fluoride (PVDF) were taken in a mass ratio 8:1:1 and mixed with 2 mL of N-methyl-2-pyrrolidinone (NMP). The suspension was applied to an aluminum-coated Mylar film and dried at 70 °C for 12 h under vacuum (10<sup>−2</sup> mbar). This electrode and the sodium plate were separated by polypropylene. The electrolyte was a 1 M NaClO<sub>4</sub> solution in EC/DMC mixture (1:1 in volume) with 5% fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC). The galvanostatic discharge of the cell was carried out using the NEWARE CT-3008 station.</p>
                  
                  <p>
For ex situ XPS and XRD experiments, a MoS<sub>2</sub>/rGO/SuperP/PVDF/NMP suspension was deposited on a copper foil and the resulting working electrode was assembled with a separator, electrolyte, and sodium plate using a conventional CR2023 cell. The measurements were performed for a fully discharged working electrode after it was washing with DEC and dried.</p>
                  </section>
               </section>
            </section>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
